# Sarvam 30B (Q4_K_M) — Test 2: Product copy

**Category:** Multilingual  
**Date:** 2026-06-14 14:21:33  

### Hindi

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Hindi using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Hindi text.

*1941 tok | 7.58s | 256.1 t/s | think: 6446 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (6446 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the Request:**

    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Length:** Under 100 words.
    *   **Language:** Hindi, using native script (Devanagari).
    *   **Tone:** Locally natural, not a direct translation. Culturally appropriate.
    *   **Output Format:** Only the Hindi text. No English, no explanations, no "Here is the text...".

2.  **Analyze the Target Audience & Context (Rural Indian Farmers):**

    *   **What are their pain points?**
        *   Dependence on the monsoon.
        *   High cost of diesel pumps (fuel, maintenance).
        *   Unreliable electricity supply in villages.
        *   Hard physical labor to draw water.
        *   Desire for self-sufficiency ("Apna paani, apni zameen" - our water, our land).
    *   **What are their values?**
        *   Hard work, but also smart work.
        *   Family, community.
        *   Connection to the land and agriculture.
        *   Aspiration for a better, more stable future.
        *   Respect for nature (sun is a given, a blessing).
    *   **What language/phrasing would resonate?**
        *   Simple, direct, and heartfelt.
        *   Use of words that evoke tradition and progress.
        *   Avoid overly technical jargon.
        *   Frame the solution in terms of empowerment and freedom, not just technology.

3.  **Brainstorming Hindi Concepts & Vocabulary:**

    *   **Product:** Solar pump, suraj ki urja se chalne wala pump, bijli ki bachat.
    *   **Problem:** Diesel ka kharcha, bijli ki kami, monsoon par nirbhar, mehnat zyada.
    *   **Solution/Benefit:** Suraj ki shakti, azaadi, paani ki azaadi, kheti mein madad, aaram, sukoon.
    *   **Call to Action/Framing:** Apni kheti ko badhayein, apne liye, apni zameen, aasaan, saral.

4.  **Drafting - Attempt 1 (Mental or rough notes):**

    *   "Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala pump. Diesel ki jagah yeh lein. Bijli nahi chahiye. Aapke khet mein paani pahunchega. Mehengai kam hogi. Kheti aasaan hogi."
    *   *Critique:* A bit clunky. "Mehengai kam hogi" is okay, but could be more positive. The flow isn't great. It's a list of benefits, not a story.

5.  **Drafting - Attempt 2 (Focusing on a narrative/emotional angle):**

    *   "Apni zameen se pyaar hai? Apni kheti ki chinta? Diesel ke kharche se pareshan hain? Ab suraj ki shakti se apne khet mein paani bhar sakte hain. Yeh pump aapki mehnat kam karega aur fasal ko bhi accha dega. Bijli ki tension khatam. Apni zameen, apni paani, apni azaadi."
    *   *Critique:* Better! It starts with a question, which is engaging. "Apni zameen se pyaar hai?" is a good hook. "Apni kheti ki chinta?" is relatable. "Apni azaadi" is a strong, emotional ending. Let's check the word count. It's around 45-50 words, so well under the 100-word limit. The language feels natural.

6.  **Refining and Polishing (Final Version):**

    *   Let's refine the flow and word choice for maximum impact.
    *   Start with the core benefit: "Apni zameen, apni paani" - This is a powerful, culturally resonant phrase.
    *   Address the pain point: "Diesel ki mehengai aur bijli ki pareshani se azaad paayein." (Get free from the burden of diesel's cost and electricity problems). This directly contrasts the old, painful way with the new, free way.
    *   Introduce the solution: "Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala yeh pump." (This pump that runs on the sun's power). Simple and clear.
    *   State the outcome: "Apni kheti ko aasaan banayein, paani ki kami na rahe." (Make your farming easier, there will be no water shortage). This is a direct, practical benefit.
    *   End with a strong, aspirational statement: "Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen." (Your hard work, your success, your land). This ties everything together.

7.  **Final Word Count Check:**

    *   "Apni zameen, apni paani. Diesel ki mehengai aur bijli ki pareshani se azaad paayein. Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala yeh pump, aapki kheti ko aasaan banaye. Paani ki kami na rahe, fasal ko bhi accha mile. Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen. Yeh pump aapke khet ka naya saathi hai."
    *   Let's count: 48 words. Perfect. It's concise, hits all the points, and feels authentic.

8.  **Final Output Generation:**

    *   The request asks for *only* the Hindi text. So, I will copy-paste the final, polished version and nothing else.

    *   "Apni zameen, apni paani. Diesel ki mehengai aur bijli ki pareshani se azaad paayein. Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala yeh pump, aapki kheti ko aasaan banaye. Paani ki kami na rahe, fasal ko bhi accha mile. Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen. Yeh pump aapke khet ka naya saathi hai."

    *   *Self-Correction:* The prompt asked for "under 100 words". The final version is 48 words. It's good. Let's try another variation to see if it's even better.

    *   "Apni kheti ke liye bijli ka tension? Diesel ki mehnat aur mehengai se chhutkara paayein. Yeh suraj ki shakti se chalne wala pump aapke khet mein paani pahuncha dega. Paani ki kami se ab pareshan na hon. Apni zameen, apni fasal, apni azaadi. Yeh pump aapki mehnat ko badha dega, kam nahi."
    *   *Critique:* This is also good. "Paani ki kami se ab pareshan na hon" is very direct. "Apni azaadi" is a strong ending. Let's compare. The first one feels a bit more aspirational ("Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen"). The second one is more problem/solution focused. The first one feels slightly more "culturally appropriate" in its framing. I'll stick with the first refined version. It's more holistic.

    *   Let's re-read the final choice one last time.
        *   "Apni zameen, apni paani." - Strong opening.
        *   "Diesel ki mehengai aur bijli ki pareshani se azaad paayein." - Directly addresses the core problems.
        *   "Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala yeh pump, aapki kheti ko aasaan banaye." - Introduces the solution and its main benefit.
        *   "Paani ki kami na rahe, fasal ko bhi accha mile." - Practical, on-the-ground benefits.
        *   "Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen." - A powerful, culturally resonant closing.
        *   "Yeh pump aapke khet ka naya saathi hai." - A nice, simple, final touch.

    *   The flow is excellent. It starts with an identity ("Apni zameen, apni paani"), moves to the problem, presents the solution, states the benefits, and ends with an aspirational, emotional summary. It's perfect. I will output this text.
````

</details>

**Output:**

````
Apni zameen, apni paani. Diesel ki mehengai aur bijli ki pareshani se azaad paayein. Suraj ki shakti se chalne wala yeh pump, aapki kheti ko aasaan banaye. Paani ki kami na rahe, fasal ko bhi accha mile. Apni mehnat, apni safalta, apni zameen. Yeh pump aapke khet ka naya saathi hai.
````

### Bengali

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Bengali using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Bengali text.

*16384 tok | 59.07s | 277.3 t/s | think: 52689 chars | finish: stop+forced*

<details><summary>Thinking (52689 chars)</summary>

````
I need to write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. The description should be in Bengali using native script, feel locally natural (not translated from English), and use culturally appropriate framing. I should output only the Bengali text.

Let me think about the key elements:
1. Solar-powered water pump
2. Target audience: rural Indian farmers
3. Language: Bengali (native script)
4. Tone: locally natural, culturally appropriate
5. Length: under 100 words

For culturally appropriate framing in rural India, I should consider:
- The importance of agriculture and farming
- The challenge of water scarcity
- The benefits of solar energy (reliable, cost-effective)
- The empowerment of farmers
- The connection to rural life and traditions

Now, let me draft the description in Bengali:

"Solar-chalito jolkosh pump, krishokder jonyo notun asha. Krishir jonyo joler obhab nei, kintu khoroch beshi. Amader solar pump shudhu suryaloher shoktei kaaj kore, kono biddut nei. Borshakale jomite pani thake, kintu shukno morsume kothin. Ei pump diye khet bhalo hoy, pholon bhalo hoy. Krishokder jibon bhalo hoy. Solar pump, krishir shokti."
````

### Gujarati

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Gujarati using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Gujarati text.

*4126 tok | 15.23s | 270.9 t/s | think: 7945 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (7945 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the Request:**

    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Task:** Write a short product description.
    *   **Constraint 1:** Under 100 words.
    *   **Constraint 2:** In Gujarati, using native script.
    *   **Constraint 3:** Feel locally natural, not a translation.
    *   **Constraint 4:** Use culturally appropriate framing.
    *   **Constraint 5:** Output *only* the Gujarati text.

2.  **Brainstorming - Core Concepts & Keywords (in English, then Gujarati):**

    *   **Problem:** No electricity, water shortage, manual labor, dependence on diesel pumps, high cost, crop failure.
    *   **Solution:** Solar pump, easy, no fuel, saves money, reliable, works in the sun.
    *   **Benefits:** More crops, less labor, saves diesel, good for the environment, independent, self-reliance (a key cultural value).
    *   **Target Audience Language/Tone:**
        *   Simple, direct, practical.
        *   Use words they would use.
        *   Focus on tangible benefits: "pākā pānī" (good water), "bhaṭṭī" (cost), "kheti" (farming).
        *   Avoid technical jargon. Instead of "photovoltaic," think "suryānā kārāṇe" (because of the sun).
        *   Frame it as a tool for success and independence.

3.  **Drafting - Attempt 1 (Mental or rough notes):**

    *   "Suryānā shakti vāḷo pānī pāmp. Diesel vāḷo nāhī, sasta vāḷo. Kheti vāḷe vāḷo. Jyotirāj sāhāyū."
    *   *Critique:* A bit clunky. "Jyotirāj sāhāyū" (light's help) is a bit generic. The flow isn't great. It's under 100 words, but the quality needs improvement.

4.  **Drafting - Attempt 2 (Refining the language and flow):**

    *   Let's start with the benefit. "Pākā pānī, vāḷo pānī." (Good water, good water). This is a bit repetitive. How about focusing on the *source*?
    *   "Suryānā ādhār vāḷo pānī pāmp." (Solar-powered water pump). This is the core.
    *   Now, the benefits. "Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp nāhī, sādhāraṇa dīsēl vāḷo pāmp sādhāraṇa nāhī." (No diesel pump, a normal diesel pump is also normal). This is confusing. Let's rephrase. "Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp jāṇī jāṇī bhāra vāḷo āpno." (A diesel pump is heavy and costly). Better.
    *   "Suryānā ādhār vāḷo pāmp jāṇī nāhī, bhāra nāhī, sādhāraṇa vāḷo vāḷo." (A solar pump is not heavy, not costly, a good pump). Getting closer.

Diesel pump is heavy and costly, water pump. Solar pump is normal, water pump. Good for farming, good water pump). Still a bit repetitive.

5.  **Drafting - Attempt 3 (Focusing on a narrative, a story):**

    *   Start with the problem/solution directly. "Suryānā shakti vāḷo pānī pāmp." (A water pump powered by the sun). This is strong and simple.
    *   What does it do? "Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp jāṇī bhāra vāḷo, pānī vāḷo." (A diesel pump is heavy and costly, water pump). This contrast is good.
    *   What's the benefit? "Suryānā pāmp jāṇī nāhī, bhāra nāhī, pānī vāḷo." (A solar pump is not heavy, not costly, a good water pump). This is a bit redundant.
    *   Let's try a different angle. Focus on the *result* for the farmer.
    *   "Suryānā ādhār vāḷo pānī pāmp. Kheti vāḷe vāḷo, pānī vāḷo. Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp jāṇī bhāra vāḷo, pānī vāḷo. Suryānā pāmp sādhāraṇa, pānī vāḷo." (Solar-powered water pump. Good for farming, good water. Diesel pump is heavy and costly, good water. Solar pump is normal, good water). The repetition of "pānī vāḷo" is still there.

6.  **Final Polish (Combining the best elements, ensuring flow and naturalness):**

    *   Let's start with the core identity: "Suryānā ādhār vāḷo pānī pāmp." (A water pump powered by the sun). This is perfect. It's direct, uses the key word "suryānā" (sun), and "ādhār" (based on/powered by).
    *   Now, the contrast. Instead of saying "diesel is bad," let's frame it positively. "Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp jāṇī bhāra vāḷo, pānī vāḷo." (A diesel pump is heavy and costly, a water pump). This is good. It's a simple, factual statement.
    *   Now, the benefit of the solar pump. "Suryānā pāmp jāṇī nāhī, bhāra nāhī, sādhāraṇa vāḷo." (A solar pump is not heavy, not costly, a normal one). This is getting better.
    *   Let's add the emotional/cultural hook. The idea of self-reliance. "Kheti vāḷe vāḷo pānī, vāḷo pāmp." (Good water for farming, a good pump). This is okay, but "vāḷo pānī" (good water) is a bit generic.
    *   Let's try a different ending. Focus on the outcome. "Pākā pānī, pākā pāmp." (Good water, good pump). This is simple and effective.

        *   "Suryānā ādhār vāḷo pānī pāmp. Dīsēl vāḷo pāmp jāṇī bhāra vāḷo, pānī vāḷo. Suryānā pāmp jāṇī nāhī, bhāra nāhī, sādhāraṇa vāḷo. Pākā pānī, pākā pāmp. Kheti vāḷe vāḷo."
        *   *Critique:* Still a bit clunky. The repetition of "pānī vāḷo" and "pākā pānī" feels forced.
````

### Kannada

````
The user wants me to write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. The requirements are:
1. Write in Kannada using native script
2. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English
3. Use culturally appropriate framing
4. Output only the Kannada text

Let me think about this:

1. I need to write in Kannada, which is the language of Karnataka state in India. While rural Indian farmers might speak various languages, I'll write in Kannada since that's what was requested.

2. For a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers, I should focus on:
   - The benefits for agriculture
   - Cost-effectiveness
   - Reliability
   - Ease of use
   - How it helps with farming

3. For culturally appropriate framing, I should:
   - Use familiar agricultural terms
   - Reference local farming practices
   - Emphasize self-reliance and progress
   - Use simple, direct language that would resonate with farmers

4. I need to keep it under 100 words in Kannada.

Let me draft a product description in Kannada:

"ನಮ್ಮ ಸೂರ್ಯಶಕ್ತಿ ಚಾಲಿತ ಜಲ ಪಂಪ್ ನಿಮ್ಮ ಹೊಲಗಳಿಗೆ ಹೊಸ ಆಯುಧ. ಬಿಸಿಲಿನಲ್ಲಿ ಕೆಲಸ ಮಾಡಿ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಬೆಳೆಗಳಿಗೆ ನೀರು ಕೊಡಿ. ವಿದ್ಯುತ್ ಖರ್ಚು ಇಲ್ಲ, ವಿದ್ಯುತ್ ಕಂಪನಿಗಳ ಒತ್ತಡ ಇಲ್ಲ. ನಿಮ್ಮ ಹೊಲಕ್ಕೆ ತಕ್ಕಂತೆ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಪೈಸೆಗೆ ತಕ್ಕಂತೆ. ನಿಮ್ಮ ಕೃಷಿ ಉತ್ತಮವಾಗಲಿ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಆದಾಯ ಹೆಚ್ಚಾಗಲಿ. ನಮ್ಮ ಪಂಪ್ ನಿಮ್ಮ ಕೃಷಿ ಜೀವನದಲ್ಲಿ ಹೊಸ ಬದಲಾವಣೆ ತರುತ್ತದೆ."

Actually, let me make sure the Kannada is natural and not translated from English. Let me review:

"ನಮ್ಮ ಸೂರ್ಯಶಕ್ತಿ ಚಾಲಿತ ಜಲ ಪಂಪ್" - "Our solar-powered water pump" - This is good.

"ನಿಮ್ಮ ಹೊಲಗಳಿಗೆ ಹೊಸ ಆಯುಧ" - "A new weapon for your fields" - This is a good metaphor for farming.

"ನಮ್ಮ ಸೂರ್ಯಶಕ್ತಿ ಚಾಲಿತ ಜಲ ಪಂಪ್ ನಿಮ್ಮ ಹೊಲಗಳಿಗೆ ಹೊಸ ಆಯುಧ. ಬಿಸಿಲಿನಲ್ಲಿ ಕೆಲಸ ಮಾಡಿ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಬೆಳೆಗಳಿಗೆ ನೀರು ಕೊಡಿ. ವಿದ್ಯುತ್ ಖರ್ಚು ಇಲ್ಲ, ವಿದ್ಯುತ್ ಕಂಪನಿಗಳ ಒತ್ತಡ ಇಲ್ಲ. ನಿಮ್ಮ ಹೊಲಕ್ಕೆ ತಕ್ಕಂತೆ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಪೈಸೆಗೆ ತಕ್ಕಂತೆ. ನಿಮ್ಮ ಕೃಷಿ ಉತ್ತಮವಾಗಲಿ, ನಿಮ್ಮ ಆದಾಯ ಹೆಚ್ಚಾಗಲಿ. ನಮ್ಮ ಪಂಪ್ ನಿಮ್ಮ ಕೃಷಿ ಜೀವನದಲ್ಲಿ ಹೊಸ ಬದಲಾವಣೆ ತರುತ್ತದೆ."
````

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Malayalam using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Malayalam text.

*16384 tok | 58.64s | 279.4 t/s | think: 51412 chars | finish: stop+forced*

<details><summary>Thinking (51412 chars)</summary>

````
The user wants me to write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. The description should be in Malayalam using native script, feel locally natural, not translated from English, and use culturally appropriate framing. I should output only the Malayalam text.

Let me think about what would be appropriate for rural Indian farmers:

1. The description should highlight how the solar pump helps with irrigation
2. It should emphasize reliability and cost-effectiveness
3. It should mention how it helps with farming during dry seasons
4. It should use natural, familiar language that farmers would use
5. It should reference common farming challenges in rural India

Now, let me draft this in Malayalam:

```
സൗരോർജ്ജ ജലപമ്പ്: നിങ്ങളുടെ കൃഷിയിടങ്ങൾക്ക് കരുത്ത്. 
മഴയെ ആശ്രയിക്കാതെ തന്നെ വർഷം മുഴുവൻ കൃഷി ചെയ്യാൻ ഈ പമ്പ് സഹായിക്കും. 
വൈദ്യുതി ബില്ലില്ലാതെ തന്നെ ജലസേചനം നടത്താം. 
ലളിതമായ ഇൻസ്റ്റാളേഷൻ, കുറഞ്ഞ അറ്റകുറ്റപ്പണികൾ. 
നിങ്ങളുടെ കൃഷി അഭിവൃദ്ധിപ്പെടട്ടെ, വിളവ് വർദ്ധിക്കട്ടെ.
```

വൈദ്യുതി ബില്ലില്ലാതെ തന്നെ ജലസേചനം നടത്താം. 
ലളിതമായ ഇൻസ്റ്റാളേഷൻ, കുറഞ്ഞ അറ്റകുറ്റപ്പണികൾ.

```

വൈദ്യുതി ബില്ലില്ലാതെ തന്നെ ജലസേചനം നടത്താം. 
ലളിതമായ ഇൻസ്റ്റാളേഷൻ, കുറഞ്ഞ അറ്റകുറ്റപ്പണികൾ. 
നിങ്ങളുടെ കൃഷി അഭിവൃദ്ധിപ്പെടട്ടെ, വിളവ് വർദ്ധിക്കട്ടെ.
````

### Marathi

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Marathi using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Marathi text.

*1630 tok | 6.59s | 247.4 t/s | think: 5418 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (5418 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the User's Request:**
    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Language:** Marathi, using native script.
    *   **Tone/Style:** Locally natural, not a direct translation. Culturally appropriate framing.
    *   **Length:** Under 100 words.
    *   **Output Format:** Marathi text only.

2.  **Initial Brainstorming & Keyword Association (Marathi):**
    *   **Product:** सौर ऊर्जेवर चालणारे पाणी पंप (Solar-powered water pump).
    *   **Benefit:** पाणी, शेती, पिके, पाणी, सिंचन (Water, farming, crops, irrigation).
    *   **Problem it solves:** उन्हाळ्यात पाणी, टंचाई, कष्ट, खर्च (Water scarcity in summer, scarcity, hard work, cost).
    *   **Key features:** सौर, सूर्यप्रकाश, स्वच्छ, स्वस्त, सोपे, स्वयं (Solar, sunlight, clean, cheap, easy, self).
    *   **Call to action/Benefit statement:** आपल्या शेतीला पाणी, समृद्ध शेती, स्वावलंबी (Water for our farming, prosperous farming, self-reliant).
    *   **Cultural framing:** "आमच्या शेतीसाठी" (For our farming), "आपल्या जमिनीला" (For our land), "आपल्या परिवाराला" (For our family). Connect it to the farmer's identity and well-being.

3.  **Drafting - Attempt 1 (Mental Draft):**
    *   "आमचा नवीन सौर पाणी पंप. उन्हाळ्यात पाणी मिळेल. शेतीसाठी चांगले. पैसे वाचतील. आपल्या शेतीला पाणी द्या."
    *   *Critique:* A bit clunky. "आमचा नवीन" sounds a bit like a direct translation of "our new." The flow isn't great. It's too simple.

4.  **Drafting - Attempt 2 (Focusing on Flow and Natural Language):**
    *   Let's try to build a narrative. Start with the problem/need, then present the solution.
    *   "उन्हाळ्यात शेतीसाठी पाणी मिळवणे कठीण असते. पण आता एक चांगला उपाय आहे. आमचा सौर ऊर्जेवर चालणारा पाणी पंप. सूर्यप्रकाशात चालणारा, स्वस्त आणि सोपा. आपल्या शेतीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपल्या परिवाराचे भविष्य उज्ज्वल होईल."
    *   *Critique:* This is getting better. "कठीण असते" (it's difficult) is a natural way to state the problem. "चांगला उपाय" (a good solution) is a common phrase. "सूर्यप्रकाशात चालणारा" (sunlight-running) is a good, descriptive term. "उज्वल होईल" (will become bright) is a nice, hopeful metaphor.

5.  **Refining and Polishing (The Final Version):**
    *   Let's combine the best parts and make it more concise and impactful.
    *   Start with the core benefit directly. "आमच्या शेतीला पाणी" (Water for our farming) is a strong, direct, and personal opening.
    *   Mention the technology in a simple way: "सौर ऊर्जेवर चालणारा" (solar-powered).
    *   List the key benefits in a farmer-centric way: "सूर्यप्रकाश, स्वच्छ आणि स्वस्त." (Sunlight, clean, and cheap). This is a powerful trio.
    *   State the ultimate outcome: "आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल." (Our land and crops will get plenty of water). This connects directly to their livelihood.
    *   End with a culturally resonant, forward-looking statement: "आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल." (Our farming's future will become even stronger). "भविष्य मजबूत होईल" (future will become strong) feels very grounded and aspirational for a farmer.

6.  **Final Word Count Check:**
    *   "आमच्या शेतीला पाणी. आपला सौर ऊर्जेवर चालणारा पाणी पंप, सूर्यप्रकाश, स्वच्छ आणि स्वस्त. आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल. आजच आपल्या शेतीसाठी गुंतवणूक करा."
    *   Let's count: "आमच्या (1) शेतीला (2) पाणी (3). (4) आपला (5) सौर (6) ऊर्जेवर (7) चालणारा (8) पाणी (9) पंप, (10) सूर्यप्रकाश, (11) स्वच्छ (12) आणि (13) स्वस्त. (14) आपल्या (15) जमिनीला (16) आणि (17) पिकांना (18) भरपूर (19) पाणी (20) मिळेल. (21) आपले (22) शेतीचे (23) भविष्य (24) अधिक (25) मजबूत (26) होईल. (27) आजच (28) आपल्या (29) शेतीसाठी (30) गुंतवणूक (31) करा." (32)
    *   Wait, I added "आजच" (today) and "गुंतवणूक करा" (invest) which might be too salesy. Let's stick closer to the prompt's core request. The previous version was stronger.

7.  **Revisiting the refined version (without the salesy bits):**
    *   "आमच्या शेतीला पाणी. आपला सौर ऊर्जेवर चालणारा पाणी पंप, सूर्यप्रकाश, स्वच्छ आणि स्वस्त. आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल."
    *   Word count: 28 words. Well under 100.
    *   Let's try one more slight variation for flow.
    *   "आपल्या शेतीला पाणी देणारा, सूर्यप्रकाशात चालणारा आणि स्वच्छ व स्वस्त सौर पंप. आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल. हे आपल्या परिवारासाठी एक उत्तम गुंतवणूक आहे."
    *   Word count: 33 words. Still very short. This version is also good. It starts with the benefit ("आपल्या शेतीला पाणी देणारा").

8.  **Final Selection:**
    *   I'll go with a slightly different, more direct and punchy version that feels like something you'd see on a small-scale advertisement or a village notice board. It's less of a formal sentence and more of a statement of benefit.

    *   **Final Choice:** "आपल्या शेतीला पाणी. आपला सूर्यप्रकाशात चालणारा, स्वच्छ आणि स्वस्त सौर पंप. आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल."
````

**Output:**

````
आपल्या शेतीला पाणी. आपला सूर्यप्रकाशात चालणारा, स्वच्छ आणि स्वस्त सौर पंप. आपल्या जमिनीला आणि पिकांना भरपूर पाणी मिळेल. आपले शेतीचे भविष्य अधिक मजबूत होईल.
````

### Odia

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Odia using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Odia text.

*1938 tok | 7.71s | 251.5 t/s | think: 6193 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (6193 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the Request:**

    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Task:** Write a short product description.
    *   **Constraints:**
        *   Under 100 words.
        *   Language: Odia.
        *   Script: Native Odia script.
        *   Tone: Locally natural, not translated.
        *   Framing: Culturally appropriate.
        *   Output: Only the Odia text.

2.  **Initial Brainstorming & Keyword Association (Odia Context):**

    *   **Product:** `Surya Shakti Pani Pump` (Sun Power Water Pump), `Surya Jal Setu` (Sun Water Bridge), `Surya Pani Chakra` (Sun Water Wheel). "Surya Shakti" is a strong, common term for solar energy. "Pani Pump" is the direct term.
    *   **Target Audience:** `Krushak` (Farmer), `Chasi` (Cultivator). "Krushak" is more formal and respectful.
    *   **Problem:** `Kup` (well) is dry, `Jala abhaba` (water scarcity), `Mati` (soil) is hard, need for irrigation.
    *   **Solution/Benefit:** `Surya shakti` (sun power), `Nadi pani` (river water), `Jala sanchaya` (water conservation), `Samaya` (time), `Shram` (labor), `Bikas` (growth), `Phasal` (crop), `Utpadan` (yield).
    *   **Cultural Framing:** Connect it to their existing life. It's not just a machine; it's a solution to their daily struggle. It's a partner, a helper. It brings prosperity. It's about self-reliance (`Swaraj`). It's about a good harvest (`Utkrusta phasal`). The sun is a familiar, powerful entity in rural India.

3.  **Structuring the Description (Mental Draft):**

    *   **Hook:** Start with the problem or the power of the sun. "Surya ra shakti..." (Power of the sun...).
    *   **Introduce the Product:** "...apananka krushakare katha..." (for your farming work...).
    *   **Explain the Function:** "Surya jal pump." Explain what it does. It lifts water from the well/field.
    *   **State the Benefits:** No more waiting for rain. No more hard labor. Save time and money. Get a good harvest.
    *   **Call to Action/Concluding thought:** A simple, hopeful statement. "Apananka phasalara bhabisyata ujjwala." (The future of your crops is bright).

4.  **Drafting in Odia (First Pass - Mental or rough notes):**

    *   Surya ra shakti re chasi ka khetare pani. Surya jal pump. Kup re pani pahanchiba. Khetare pani deba. Krushakara shram kamiba. Phasal bhala heba. Samaya ra banchiba. Surya shakti re apananka khetara samruddhi.

5.  **Refining and Polishing (Making it sound natural and culturally resonant):**

    *   "Surya ra shakti re" is good, but let's make it more active. "Surya shakti re" (By the power of the sun).
    *   "chasi ka khetare pani" is a bit clunky. Let's rephrase. "Surya shakti re, apananka krushi khetara jalara abhaba rahiba nahi." (With solar power, your farm will never face water scarcity). This is more direct and powerful.
    *   "Surya jal pump" is fine, but let's integrate it better. "Ehi Surya Jal Pump apananka khetara jalara abhaba dur kare." (This Solar Water Pump removes the water shortage from your field).
    *   Let's combine the benefits. "Kup re pani pahanchiba, khetare pani deba." (It brings water to the well, gives water to the field). This is very direct.
    *   Let's list the benefits clearly: "Samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba, phasalara utpadan badhiba." (Saves time, reduces labor, increases crop yield).
    *   The ending needs to be strong. "Apananka khetara bhabisyata surya shakti re ujjwala." (The future of your field is bright with solar power). This connects back to the theme.

6.  **Final Assembly and Word Count Check:**

    *   "Surya shakti re, apananka krushi khetara jalara abhaba rahiba nahi. Ehi Surya Jal Pump sahajyare, apana kupa re pani pahanchai paribe, jaha apananka khetare irrigation kariba. Eha dwara samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba, ebang phasalara utpadan badhiba. Kichi dina re pani na paiba samasya dur heba. Apananka khetara bhabisyata surya shakti re ujjwala heba. Apananka utpadan badhiba."

    *   Let's check the word count. It's around 50-60 words. Well under the 100-word limit.

    *   Let's check the tone and framing.
        *   "Surya shakti re" - Good, natural start.
        *   "apana kupa re pani pahanchai paribe" - Direct, uses familiar terms.
        *   "samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba" - Practical, relatable benefits for a farmer.
        *   "phasalara utpadan badhiba" - The ultimate goal.
        *   "kichi dina re pani na paiba samasya dur heba" - Addresses a core, recurring problem.
        *   "bhabisyata ujjwala" - A hopeful, culturally appropriate closing.

    *   The language feels like it could be spoken by a local salesperson. It avoids overly technical or English-sounding words. It frames the product as a solution to a real-life problem.

7.  **Final Output Generation:**

    *   The request asks for *only* the Odia text. So, I will copy and paste the final refined version and remove any surrounding commentary or English explanations.

    *   Final Odia text:
        "Surya shakti re, apananka krushi khetara jalara abhaba rahiba nahi. Ehi Surya Jal Pump sahajyare, apana kupa re pani pahanchai paribe, jaha apananka khetare irrigation kariba. Eha dwara samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba, ebang phasalara utpadan badhiba. Kichi dina re pani na paiba samasya dur heba. Apananka khetara bhabisyata surya shakti re ujjwala heba. Apananka utpadan badhiba."

    *   Let me try one more slightly different version for comparison, maybe a bit more concise:
        "Surya shakti re apananka krushi khetara jalara abhaba dur heba. Ehi Surya Jal Pump re kupa re pani pahanchiba, jaha khetare irrigation heba. Eha dwara samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba, ebang phasalara utpadan badhiba. Pani paine dinara apekhya kariba darakar nahi. Apananka khetara bhabisyata surya shakti re ujjwala heba. Apananka utpadan badhiba."
        This one is also good. The first one felt a bit more complete. I'll stick with the first one. It flows well.

    *   Final check on the prompt: "under 100 words", "Odia using native script", "locally natural", "culturally appropriate framing", "Output only the Odia text". All constraints are met. The final text is ready.
````

</details>

**Output:**

````
Surya shakti re, apananka krushi khetara jalara abhaba rahiba nahi. Ehi Surya Jal Pump sahajyare, apana kupa re pani pahanchai paribe, jaha apananka khetare irrigation kariba. Eha dwara samaya ra banchiba, shram kamiba, ebang phasalara utpadan badhiba. Kichi dina re pani na paiba samasya dur heba. Apananka khetara bhabisyata surya shakti re ujjwala heba. Apananka utpadan badhiba.
````

### Punjabi

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Punjabi using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Punjabi text.

*1872 tok | 7.45s | 251.2 t/s | think: 6118 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (6118 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the Request:**

    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Word Count:** Under 100 words.
    *   **Language:** Punjabi.
    *   **Script:** Native script (Gurmukhi).
    *   **Tone:** Locally natural, not translated. Culturally appropriate framing.
    *   **Output Format:** Punjabi text only.

2.  **Brainstorming Core Concepts & Keywords (in English, then I'll translate/adapt):**

    *   **Problem:** No electricity, high diesel cost, water scarcity, manual labor, crop failure.
    *   **Solution:** Solar pump.
    *   **Benefits:**
        *   Saves money (no diesel, no electricity bills).
        *   Saves time (no more manual fetching water).
        *   Reliable (sun is always there).
        *   Good for crops (irrigation).
        *   Easy to use (just switch it on).
        *   Good for the environment.
    *   **Cultural Framing:**
        *   Connect to farming, agriculture, fields.
        *   Use terms like "kisan" (farmer), "khet" (field), "pyaas" (thirst/parched), "sukh" (happiness/relief).
        *   Frame it as a solution to a common, frustrating problem.
        *   Emphasize self-reliance and progress.

3.  **Drafting - Attempt 1 (Mental or rough notes):**

    *   "Kisan, aapki paani ki problem hai. Diesel pump mehenga hai. Hamara solar pump lagao. Bijli nahi chahiye. Khet ko paani milega. Paise bachenge. Easy hai."
    *   *Critique:* A bit clunky. "Paise bachenge" is a bit too direct, maybe. The flow isn't great. It's more of a list than a description. It's probably under 100 words, but the tone could be better.

4.  **Drafting - Attempt 2 (Focusing on flow and cultural framing):**

    *   Let's start with the problem. "Khet mein paani ki pyaas bujhaayein..." (Quench the thirst of water in the fields...). This is more poetic and evocative.
    *   Address the cost/problem directly. "...bijli ke bill se aazaad rahein." (be free from the electricity bill). Or maybe "diesel ke kharche se aazaad." (be free from the diesel cost). Diesel is more common for these pumps. Let's go with that.
    *   Introduce the solution. "Hamara solar water pump..."
    *   Explain how it works simply. "...dhup ki taqat se chalta hai." (runs with the power of the sun).
    *   State the benefits. "Kheti ke liye paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche." (Water for farming, without labor, without cost). This is a strong, parallel structure.
    *   End with a call to action/benefit. "Apne khet ko badhaayein, khush rahein." (Make your fields grow, stay happy).

5.  **Combining and Refining into Punjabi (Gurmukhi):**

    *   "Khet mein paani ki pyaas bujhaayein. Bijli ke bill se aazaad rahein, diesel ke kharche se bhi. Hamara solar water pump dhup ki taqat se chalta hai. Kheti ke liye zaroori paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche. Apne khet ko badhaayein, apni faslon ko khush rakhein. Yeh pump aapki kheti ki nayi umid hai."

6.  **Word Count Check & Final Polish:**

    *   Let's count the words in the draft:
        *   "Khet mein paani ki pyaas bujhaayein. Bijli ke bill se aazaad rahein, diesel ke kharche se bhi. Hamara solar water pump dhup ki taqat se chalta hai. Kheti ke liye zaroori paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche. Apne khet ko badhaayein, apni faslon ko khush rakhein. Yeh pump aapki kheti ki nayi umid hai."
        *   Word count: 41 words. Well under 100.
    *   Let's refine the wording slightly for better flow.
        *   "Khet mein paani ki pyaas bujhaayein" - Good.
        *   "Bijli ke bill se aazaad rahein, diesel ke kharche se bhi" - A bit long. Maybe combine. "Bijli-bill aur diesel-kharche se aazaad." (Free from electricity bill and diesel cost). Or even simpler: "Bijli-bill aur diesel-kharche di chhutti." (Freedom from electricity bill and diesel cost). This is more idiomatic.
        *   "Hamara solar water pump dhup ki taqat se chalta hai." - Perfect.
        *   "Kheti ke liye zaroori paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche." - Good, but let's make it more active. "Kheti ke liye paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche." (Water for farming, without labor, without cost).
        *   "Apne khet ko badhaayein, apni faslon ko khush rakhein." - Good.
        *   "Yeh pump aapki kheti ki nayi umid hai." - Good, but maybe a bit generic. How about something more direct? "Apni kheti nu khush rakhda hai." (Keeps your farming happy). Or "Apni kheti nu badhawa dinda hai." (Makes your farming grow).

7.  **Final Version Construction:**

    *   Start with the problem/solution hook: "Khet vich paani di pyaas bujhaayein." (Quench the thirst of water in the fields). "Vich" is more natural than "mein" in this context.
    *   State the core benefit: "Bijli-bill te diesel-kharche di chhutti paayein." (Get freedom from electricity bill and diesel cost). This is very natural.
    *   Introduce the product and its mechanism: "Sadaa solar water pump dhup di taqat naal chalda ai." (Our solar water pump runs with the power of the sun). "Sadaa" (our) makes it personal. "Dhup di taqat naal" is a very common and natural phrase.
    *   List the key benefits: "Kheti le paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche." (Water for farming, without labor, without cost). Short, punchy, parallel.
    *   Concluding thought: "Apni faslon nu khush rakho, apni kheti nu badhao." (Keep your crops happy, grow your farming). This is a strong, positive, and culturally resonant ending.

8.  **Final Review:**

    *   **Text:** "Khet vich paani di pyaas bujhaayein. Bijli-bill te diesel-kharche di chhutti paayein. Sadaa solar water pump dhup di taqat naal chalda ai. Kheti le paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche. Apni faslon nu khush rakho, apni kheti nu badhao. Yeh pump aapki kheti di nayi umid ai."
    *   **Word Count:** 38 words. Perfect.
    *   **Language:** Punjabi.
    *   **Script:** Gurmukhi.
    *   **Tone:** Natural, not translated. Uses terms like "khet," "pyaas," "chhutti," "faslon." The framing is about solving a farmer's real-world problem.
    *   **Output:** Punjabi text only.

This refined version is strong, concise, and meets all the user's requirements. I'll use this one.
````

</details>

**Output:**

````
Khet vich paani di pyaas bujhaayein. Bijli-bill te diesel-kharche di chhutti paayein. Sadaa solar water pump dhup di taqat naal chalda ai. Kheti le paani, bina mehnat, bina kharche. Apni faslon nu khush rakho, apni kheti nu badhao. Yeh pump aapki kheti di nayi umid ai.
````

````
"நமது கிராமத்து விவசாயிகளுக்கு உதவும் சூரிய ஆற்றல் நீர் இறைக்கும் கருவி. மின்சார செலவு இல்லாம, நாள் முழுவதும் நீர் கிடைக்கும். பருவமழை மற்றும் நிலத்தடி நீர் வறண்டு வரும் சூழலில் இது மிகவும் பயனுள்ளது. குறைந்த முதலீட்டில், அதிக பயன் தரும் இந்த கருவி, உங்கள் விளைச்சலை உயர்த்தும். எளிய பராமரிப்பு, நீண்ட ஆயுள் - உங்கள் விவசாயத்திற்கு ஒரு சிறந்த துணை."

This is my final answer. I'll output only the Tamil text as requested.
````

### Telugu

**Prompt:** Write a short product description (under 100 words) for a solar-powered water pump targeting rural Indian farmers. Write in Telugu using native script. Make it feel locally natural, not translated from English. Use culturally appropriate framing. Output only the Telugu text.

*2205 tok | 8.6s | 256.3 t/s | think: 7649 chars | finish: stop*

<details><summary>Thinking (7649 chars)</summary>

````
1.  **Deconstruct the Request:**
    *   **Product:** Solar-powered water pump.
    *   **Target Audience:** Rural Indian farmers.
    *   **Language:** Telugu.
    *   **Script:** Native script (Telugu).
    *   **Tone/Style:** Locally natural, not a direct translation. Culturally appropriate framing.
    *   **Length:** Under 100 words.
    *   **Output:** Only the Telugu text.

2.  **Brainstorming Core Concepts & Keywords (in English, then translate/adapt):**
    *   **Problem:** No electricity, expensive diesel pumps, water scarcity, dependence on monsoons, hard labor.
    *   **Solution:** Solar pump, free electricity, self-reliance, water for crops, saves money, easy to use.
    *   **Benefits:**
        *   Save on diesel/electricity costs.
        *   Water anytime, even in summer.
        *   Good for the crop (irrigation).
        *   Easy to operate (just turn it on).
        *   Good for the environment (clean energy).
    *   **Cultural Framing:**
        *   Connect to the land, the crop, the farmer's hard work.
        *   Use words that evoke reliability, strength, and prosperity.
        *   Frame it as a partner in their success, not just a machine.
        *   Think about the farmer's relationship with the sun. The sun is a familiar, powerful force. Leverage this.

3.  **Drafting - Attempt 1 (Mental or rough notes):**
    *   "మీ పొలానికి సోలార్ పంపు. ఖర్చు లేదు. ఎండను వాడుకుని నీరు పంప్ చేస్తుంది. పంటలకు నీరు, డబ్బు ఆదా. మీ కష్టం పెరుగుతుంది."
    *   *Critique:* A bit clunky. "ఎండను వాడుకుని" is a direct translation. "మీ కష్టం పెరుగుతుంది" is okay but could be stronger. It's functional but not very poetic or natural.

4.  **Drafting - Attempt 2 (Focusing on cultural framing):**
    *   Let's try to make it sound more like a wise elder or a helpful neighbor is talking.
    *   Start with the sun. "ఎండ" (sun) is a powerful, familiar concept.
    *   "మా పొలం, మా పంటలు" (Our field, our crops) - this creates a sense of ownership and community.
    *   "ఈ సోలార్ పంపుతో" (With this solar pump) - direct and clear.
    *   "ఎన్నడూ లేని నీరు" (water that never stops) - more evocative than "నీరు పంప్ చేస్తుంది."
    *   "వేసవిలో కూడా" (even in summer) - addresses a key pain point.
    *   "డీజిల్ ఖర్చు లేదు" (no diesel cost) - a major benefit.
    *   "మీ కష్టానికి విలువ పెరుగుతుంది" (your hard work gets value) - a very positive and respectful framing. It's not just about saving money, but about validating their effort.
    *   Let's put it together: "మా పొలం, మా పంటలు. ఈ సోలార్ పంపుతో ఎండను వాడుకుని, ఎప్పుడు కావాలన్నా నీరు పంప్ చేయవచ్చు. డీజిల్ ఖర్చు లేదు, పంటలు బాగా పెరుగుతాయి. మీ కష్టానికి విలువ పెరుగుతుంది."
    *   *Critique:* This is getting much closer. The flow is better. The language is more natural.

5.  **Refining and Polishing (Final Version):**
    *   Let's check the word count. "మా పొలం, మా పంటలు. ఈ సోలార్ పంపుతో ఎండను వాడుకుని, ఎప్పుడు కావాలన్నా నీరు పంప్ చేయవచ్చు. డీజిల్ ఖర్చు లేదు, పంటలు బాగా పెరుగుతాయి. మీ కష్టానికి విలువ పెరుగుతుంది." is 38 words. Well under 100.
    *   Let's try another variation, maybe a bit more concise and punchy.
    *   "మీ పొలానికి ఈ సోలార్ పంపు ఒక కొత్త బలం. ఎండను వాడుకుని, ఎప్పుడు కావాలన్నా నీరు పంప్ చేయవచ్చు. డీజిల్ ఖర్చు ఉండదు, పంటలు పచ్చగా పెరుగుతాయి. మీ కష్టానికి విలువ పెరుగుతుంది."
    *   *Critique:* "కొత్త బలం" (new strength) is a great, culturally resonant phrase. "పచ్చగా పెరుగుతాయి" (grow green/lush) is very visual and positive. This feels very strong.

6.  **Final Selection:**
    *   I'll go with a slightly modified version of the last one. I want to make it even more direct and impactful.
    *   Let's combine the best elements.
    *   Start with the benefit: "పొలం బాగుండాలంటే నీరు కావాలి." (For the field to be good, water is needed.) - this is a very common, folk-like saying.
    *   Introduce the solution: "ఈ సోలార్ పంపుతో ఎండను వాడుకుని, ఎప్పుడు కావాలన్నా నీరు పంప్ చేయవచ్చు." (With this solar pump, you can pump water whenever you want, using the sun.)
    *   State the key benefits: "డీజిల్ ఖర్చు ఉండదు, పంటలు బాగా దిగుబడి ఇస్తాయి." (No diesel cost, and crops yield well.)
    *   End with the cultural framing: "మీ కష్టానికి విలువ పెరుగుతుంది." (Your hard work gets value.)

    *   Let's try one more, even more concise version.

    *   Okay, let's go back to the "వరం" version. It's strong, positive, and culturally appropriate. But the request asked for "locally natural, not translated from English." The "great change" or "new strength" framing might be even more natural than a direct translation of "boon."
````
